     <p><b>Cornell University</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɔr/ 'or' in 'born'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɔr</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɛ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'l' in 'lie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">l</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling" class="Unicode"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Wikipedia:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>kor-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span class="SMALLCAPS" style="FONT-VARIANT:SMALL-CAPS;"><span class="NOCAPS" style="TEXT-TRANSFORM:LOWERCASE;">NEL</span></span></span></b></i></a></span>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a> <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education#Doctorate-granting_Universities" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Founded in 1865 by <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Cornell" title="Ezra Cornell">Ezra Cornell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dickson_White" title="Andrew Dickson White">Andrew Dickson White</a>, the university was intended to teach and make contributions in all fields of knowledge — from the <a href="/wiki/Classics" title="Classics">classics</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">sciences</a>, and from the theoretical to the applied. These ideals, unconventional for the time, are captured in Cornell's motto, a popular 1865 Ezra Cornell quotation: &quot;I would found an institution where any person can find instruction in any study.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-motto_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motto-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is broadly organized into seven <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> colleges and seven <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate</a> divisions at its main Ithaca campus, with each college and division defining its own admission standards and academic programs in near autonomy. The university also administers two satellite medical campuses, one in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and one in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>. Cornell is one of two private <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land grant universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>note 1<span>]</span></a></sup> Of its seven undergraduate colleges, three are <a href="/wiki/Statutory_college" title="Statutory college">state-supported statutory or contract colleges</a>, including its agricultural and veterinary colleges. As a land grant college, it operates a <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_extension" title="Cooperative extension" class="mw-redirect">cooperative extension</a> outreach program in every county of New York and receives annual funding from the State of New York for certain educational missions.<sup id="cite_ref-Spitzer_2005_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spitzer_2005-7"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The Cornell University Ithaca Campus spans over 2,300 acres, but in actuality, is much larger due to the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Plantations" title="Cornell Plantations">Cornell Plantations</a> (more than 3,000 acres) as well as the numerous university owned lands in New York.</p> 
     <p>Since its founding, Cornell has been a <a href="/wiki/Co-education" title="Co-education" class="mw-redirect">co-educational</a>, non-<a href="/wiki/Sectarianism" title="Sectarianism">sectarian</a> institution where admission is offered irrespective of religion or race. Cornell counts more than 245,000 living <a href="/wiki/Alumnus" title="Alumnus">alumni</a>, 31&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholarship" title="Marshall Scholarship">Marshall Scholars</a>, 28&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_Cornell_University" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with Cornell University">41 Nobel laureates</a> as affiliated with the university.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nobel_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rhodes_Scholars_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhodes_Scholars-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The student body consists of nearly 14,000 undergraduate and 7,000 graduate students from all 50 American states and 122 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-student_body_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-student_body-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td> 
         <div id="toctitle"> 
          <h2>Contents</h2> 
         </div> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Campuses"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Campuses</span></a> 
           <ul>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cornell_University" title="History of Cornell University">History of Cornell University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell University was founded on April&nbsp;27, 1865 as the result of a <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Senate" title="New York State Senate">New York State (NYS) Senate</a> bill that named the university as the state's <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land grant</a> institution. Senator <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Cornell" title="Ezra Cornell">Ezra Cornell</a> offered his farm in <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca, New York</a> as a site and $500,000 of his personal fortune as an initial <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">endowment</a>. Fellow senator and experienced educator <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dickson_White" title="Andrew Dickson White">Andrew Dickson White</a> agreed to be the first president. During the next three years, White oversaw the construction of the initial two buildings and traveled around the globe to attract students and <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(university)" title="Faculty (university)" class="mw-redirect">faculty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-founding_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-founding-11"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was inaugurated on October 7, 1868, and 412 men were enrolled the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-opening_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opening-12"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright" style="width: 306px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div style="clear: both; font-weight: bold; text-align: center; background-color:"> 
        <p>Cornell's founders</p> 
       </div> 
       <div style="float: left; margin: 1px; width: 147px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ezra_Cornell.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ezra_Cornell.jpg/145px-Ezra_Cornell.jpg" width="145" height="184" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ezra_Cornell.jpg/218px-Ezra_Cornell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Ezra_Cornell.jpg/290px-Ezra_Cornell.jpg 2x" /></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Cornell" title="Ezra Cornell">Ezra Cornell</a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="float: left; margin: 1px; width: 147px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg/145px-Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg" width="145" height="185" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg/218px-Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg/290px-Andrew_Dickson_White_1885.jpg 2x" /></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dickson_White" title="Andrew Dickson White">Andrew Dickson White</a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell continued to be a technological innovator applying its research to its own campus as well as to outreach efforts. For example, it was one of the first university campuses to use electricity to light the grounds from a water-powered <a href="/wiki/Dynamo" title="Dynamo">dynamo</a> in 1883.<sup id="cite_ref-chp_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chp-13"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1894, Cornell has included state-funded statutory colleges<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> and has also administered research and extension activities that have been jointly funded by state and federal matching funds.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Cornell has had an active alumni since its earliest classes and was one of the first universities to include alumni-elected representatives on its Board of Trustees.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>note 2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell expanded significantly, particularly since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War&nbsp;II</a>, with its student population in Ithaca growing to its current count of about 20,000 students. The faculty also expanded, and by the century's end, the university had more than 3,400&nbsp;faculty members.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>note 3<span>]</span></a></sup> The school also increased its breadth of course offerings. Today the university has wide-ranging programs and offers more than 4,000&nbsp;courses.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell received national attention in April&nbsp;1969 when African American students occupied <a href="/wiki/Willard_Straight_Hall" title="Willard Straight Hall">Willard Straight Hall</a> in protest over alleged racism.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The crisis resulted in the resignation of President <a href="/wiki/James_A._Perkins" title="James A. Perkins" class="mw-redirect">James A. Perkins</a> and the restructuring of university governance.<sup id="cite_ref-Downs1999_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Downs1999-20"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 2000, Cornell has been expanding its <a href="#International_programs">international programs</a>. In 2004, the university opened the <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College_in_Qatar" title="Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar">Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar</a>, the first American <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a> outside of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutqatar_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutqatar-21"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> It continues to forge partnerships with major institutions in India, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and the People's Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The university, with its high international profile, claims to be &quot;the first <a href="/wiki/International" title="International">transnational</a> university&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-transnational_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transnational-25"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> On March&nbsp;9, 2004, Cornell and Stanford laid the cornerstone for a new Bridging the Rift Center located on the Israel–Jordan border.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG/220px-Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG/330px-Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG/440px-Cornell_University_arts_quad.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption">

        <a href="/wiki/McGraw_Tower" title="McGraw Tower" class="mw-redirect">McGraw Tower</a> in the background
       </div>

     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        <a href="/wiki/Sage_Chapel" title="Sage Chapel">Sage Chapel</a> hosts religious services and concerts, and is the final resting place of the university's founders
       </div>

     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ithaca_campus">Ithaca campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ithaca campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Central_Campus" title="Cornell Central Campus">Cornell Central Campus</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus" title="Cornell North Campus">Cornell North Campus</a>, and 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_West_Campus" title="Cornell West Campus">Cornell West Campus</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell's main campus is on East Hill in <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca, New York</a>, overlooking the town and <a href="/wiki/Cayuga_Lake" title="Cayuga Lake">Cayuga Lake</a>. When the university was founded in 1865, the campus consisted of 209.5&nbsp;acres (0.85&nbsp;km&sup2;) of Ezra Cornell's roughly 300&nbsp;acre (1.2&nbsp;km&sup2;) farm.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Since then, it has swelled to about 2300&nbsp;acres (3.0&nbsp;km&sup2;), encompassing both the hill and much of the surrounding areas.<sup id="cite_ref-ithaca_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ithaca-27"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Some 260 university buildings are divided primarily between <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Central_Campus" title="Cornell Central Campus">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus" title="Cornell North Campus">North Campuses</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> of the Hill, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_West_Campus" title="Cornell West Campus">West Campus</a> on its slope, and Collegetown immediately south of Central Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-ithaca_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ithaca-27"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Central Campus has laboratories, administrative buildings, and almost all of the campus' academic buildings, athletic facilities, auditoriums, and museums. The only remaining residential facility on Central Campus is the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Law_School" title="Cornell Law School">Law School's</a> dormitory, Hughes Hall. North Campus contains <a href="/wiki/Freshman" title="Freshman">freshman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student" class="mw-redirect">graduate student</a> housing, themed program houses, and 29&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fraternity_and_sorority_houses" title="Fraternity and sorority houses" class="mw-redirect">fraternity and sorority houses</a>. West Campus has upperclass residential colleges and an additional 25&nbsp;fraternity and sorority houses.<sup id="cite_ref-map_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map-28"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Collegetown contains two upperclass <a href="/wiki/Residence_halls" title="Residence halls" class="mw-redirect">residence halls</a><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Schwartz <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">Performing Arts</a> Center amid a neighborhood of apartments, eateries, and businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The main campus is marked by an irregular layout and eclectic <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">architectural styles</a>, including ornate <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic" class="mw-redirect">Collegiate Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neoclassical</a> buildings, and less decorative <a href="/wiki/International_style_(architecture)" title="International style (architecture)" class="mw-redirect">international</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist</a> structures. The more ornate buildings generally predate <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Because the student population doubled from 7,000 in 1950 to 15,000 by 1970, grandiosity was neglected in favor of less expensive and more rapidly constructed styles.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> While some buildings are neatly arranged into <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangles</a>, others are packed densely and haphazardly. These eccentricities arose from the university's numerous, ever-changing master plans for the campus. For example, in one of the earliest plans, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a>, the designer of <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>, outlined a &quot;grand terrace&quot; overlooking <a href="/wiki/Cayuga_Lake" title="Cayuga Lake">Cayuga Lake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Because the terrace plan was dropped, McGraw Hall appears to face the wrong direction, facing Libe Slope rather than the Arts Quad.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>The university is home to several buildings on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dickson_White_House" title="Andrew Dickson White House">Andrew Dickson White House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bailey_Hall_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="Bailey Hall (Ithaca, New York)">Bailey Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caldwell_Hall_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="Caldwell Hall (Ithaca, New York)">Caldwell Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comstock_Hall_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="Comstock Hall (Ithaca, New York)">Comstock Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morrill_Hall" title="Morrill Hall">Morrill Hall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deke_House_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="Deke House (Ithaca, New York)">Deke House</a>. At least three other historic buildings—<a href="/wiki/Roberts_Hall_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="Roberts Hall (Ithaca, New York)">the original Roberts Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Robert_Hall_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="East Robert Hall (Ithaca, New York)" class="mw-redirect">East Robert Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stone_Hall_(Ithaca,_New_York)" title="Stone Hall (Ithaca, New York)">Stone Hall</a>—have also been listed on the NRHP, despite their demolitions in the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Ithaca Campus is among the rolling valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Finger_Lakes" title="Finger Lakes">Finger Lakes</a> region and, atop East Hill, provides a view of the surrounding area, including 38&nbsp;miles (61.4&nbsp;km) long <a href="/wiki/Lake_Cayuga" title="Lake Cayuga" class="mw-redirect">Lake Cayuga</a>. Two <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">gorges</a>, Fall Creek Gorge and Cascadilla Gorge, bound Central Campus and become popular swimming holes during the warmer months (although the university discourages their use).<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Adjacent to the main campus, Cornell owns the 2,800&nbsp;acre (11.6&nbsp;km&sup2;) <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Plantations" title="Cornell Plantations">Cornell Plantations</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> containing flowers, trees, and ponds along manicured trails.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell has adopted a comprehensive sustainability action plan, and has a number<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="You can help — (April 2013)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup> of <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design</a> (LEED) certified buildings on the Ithaca campus.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2009, a new gas-fired combined heat and power facility replaced a coal-fired steam plant, resulting in a reduction in carbon emissions to 7% below 1990 levels, and to reduce carbon dioxide emissions by 75,000 tons per year.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The facility meets 15% of campus electrical needs,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> and a university-run, on-campus hydroelectric plant in the Fall Creek Gorge provides an additional 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has a <a href="/wiki/Deep_lake_water_cooling" title="Deep lake water cooling" class="mw-redirect">lake source cooling</a> project that uses Lake Cayuga to air condition campus buildings, with an 80% energy saving over conventional systems.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, Cornell established a Center for a Sustainable Future.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell has been rated &quot;A-&quot; by the 2011 College Sustainability Report Card for its environmental and sustainability initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_City_campuses">New York City campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: New York City campuses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cornell_Weill">Cornell Weill</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cornell Weill">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_med_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Cornell_med_02.jpg/220px-Cornell_med_02.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Cornell_med_02.jpg/330px-Cornell_med_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Cornell_med_02.jpg/440px-Cornell_med_02.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_med_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Weill_Medical_Center" title="Weill Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">Weill Medical Center</a> overlooks the East River in 
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell's medical campus in New York, also called Weill Cornell, is on the <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. It is home to two Cornell divisions, <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College_of_Cornell_University" title="Weill Cornell Medical College of Cornell University" class="mw-redirect">Weill Cornell Medical College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Graduate_School_of_Medical_Sciences" title="Weill Cornell Graduate School of Medical Sciences">Weill Cornell Graduate School of Medical Sciences</a>, and has been affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/NewYork%E2%80%93Presbyterian_Hospital" title="NewYork–Presbyterian Hospital">NewYork–Presbyterian Hospital</a> since 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Although their faculty and academic divisions are separate, the Medical Center shares its administrative and teaching hospital functions with the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University_Medical_Center" title="Columbia University Medical Center">Columbia University Medical Center</a>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These teaching hospitals also include the Payne Whitney Clinic in Manhattan and the Westchester Division in <a href="/wiki/White_Plains,_New_York" title="White Plains, New York">White Plains, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Weill Cornell Medical College is also affiliated with the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Sloan%E2%80%93Kettering_Cancer_Center" title="Memorial Sloan–Kettering Cancer Center">Memorial Sloan–Kettering Cancer Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">Rockefeller University</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_for_Special_Surgery" title="Hospital for Special Surgery">Hospital for Special Surgery</a>. Many faculty members have joint appointments at these institutions, and Weill Cornell, Rockefeller, and Memorial Sloan–Kettering offer the <a href="/wiki/Tri-Institutional_MD%E2%80%93PhD_Program" title="Tri-Institutional MD–PhD Program">Tri-Institutional MD–PhD Program</a> to selected entering Cornell medical students.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1942 to 1979, the campus also housed a Cornell school of nursing.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cornell_NYC_Tech">Cornell NYC Tech</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cornell NYC Tech">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_NYC_Tech" title="Cornell NYC Tech">Cornell NYC Tech</a>
     </div> 
     <p>On December 19, 2011, a bid by a consortium of Cornell University and <a href="/wiki/Technion-Israel_Institute_of_Technology" title="Technion-Israel Institute of Technology" class="mw-redirect">Technion-Israel Institute of Technology</a> won a competition for rights to claim free city land as well as $100 million in subsidies to build an engineering campus in the city. The competition was established by New York City Mayor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg" title="Michael Bloomberg">Michael Bloomberg</a> in order to increase entrepreneurship and job growth in the city's technology sector. The winning bid consisted of a 2.1 million square feet state-of-the-art tech campus to be built on <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island" title="Roosevelt Island">Roosevelt Island</a> on the site of the <a href="/wiki/Coler-Goldwater_Specialty_Hospital" title="Coler-Goldwater Specialty Hospital">Coler-Goldwater Specialty Hospital</a>. Instruction began in the fall of 2012 in a temporary location in Manhattan (<a href="/wiki/111_Eighth_Avenue" title="111 Eighth Avenue">111 Eighth Avenue</a> in space donated by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thom_Mayne" title="Thom Mayne">Thom Mayne</a> of the architecture firm Morphosis has been selected to design the first building to be constructed on Roosevelt Island. Construction would begin in 2014 with a target completion for the start of the 2017 academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_New_York_City_programs">Other New York City programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other New York City programs">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In addition to the tech campus and medical center, New York City hosts local offices for some of Cornell's service programs. The Cornell Urban Scholars Program encourages students to pursue public service careers with organizations working with New York City's poorest children, families, and communities.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Human_Ecology" title="Cornell University College of Human Ecology">NYS College of Human Ecology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Agriculture_and_Life_Sciences" title="Cornell University College of Agriculture and Life Sciences">NYS College of Agriculture and Life Sciences</a> provide means for students to reach out to local communities by gardening and building with the Cornell Cooperative Extension.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Students with the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_School_of_Industrial_and_Labor_Relations" title="Cornell University School of Industrial and Labor Relations">NYS School of Industrial and Labor Relations'</a> Extension &amp; Outreach Program make workplace expertise available to organizations, union members, policy makers, and working adults.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Engineering" title="Cornell University College of Engineering">College of Engineering's</a> Operations Research Manhattan, in the city's <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Manhattan" title="Financial District, Manhattan">financial district</a>, brings together business optimization research and decision support services addressed to both financial applications and public health logistics planning.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/College_of_Architecture,_Art,_and_Planning" title="College of Architecture, Art, and Planning" class="mw-redirect">College of Architecture, Art, and Planning</a> has a facility on West 17th Street, near <a href="/wiki/Union_Square_(New_York_City)" title="Union Square (New York City)">Union Square</a>, to provide studio and seminar space for students and faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qatar_campus">Qatar campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Qatar campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:File_Upload_Wizard?wpDestFile=WCMCQ.jpg" class="new" title="File:WCMCQ.jpg">File:WCMCQ.jpg</a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        Weill Cornell Medical College in 
        <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City, Qatar</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College_in_Qatar" title="Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar">Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Weill Cornell Medical College in <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Education_City,_Qatar" title="Education City, Qatar" class="mw-redirect">Education City</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>. Opened in September 2004, it was the first American medical school outside the United States. The college is part of Cornell's program to increase its international influence. The College is a joint initiative with the Qatar government, which seeks to improve the country's academic programs and medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutqatar_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutqatar-21"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Along with its full four-year MD program, which mirrors the curriculum taught at <a href="/wiki/Weill_Medical_College" title="Weill Medical College" class="mw-redirect">Weill Medical College</a> in New York City, the college offers a two-year undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Pre-medical" title="Pre-medical">pre-medical</a> program with a separate admissions process. This undergraduate program opened in September 2002 and was the first <a href="/wiki/Coeducation" title="Coeducation" class="mw-redirect">coeducational</a> institute of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> in Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The college is partially funded by the Qatar government through the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Foundation" title="Qatar Foundation">Qatar Foundation</a>, which contributed $750 million for its construction.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The medical center is housed in a large two-story structure designed by <a href="/wiki/Arata_Isozaki" title="Arata Isozaki">Arata Isozaki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, the Qatar Foundation announced the construction of a 350-bed Specialty Teaching Hospital near the medical college in Education City. The hospital is currently under construction and is slated to be completed in the next few years.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutqatar_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutqatar-21"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Cornell University owns and operates many facilities around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory" title="Arecibo Observatory">Arecibo Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, site of the world's largest single-dish <a href="/wiki/Radio_telescope" title="Radio telescope">radio telescope</a>, was operated by Cornell under a contract with the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> from its construction until 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shoals_Marine_Laboratory" title="Shoals Marine Laboratory">Shoals Marine Laboratory</a>, operated in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Hampshire" title="University of New Hampshire">University of New Hampshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> is a seasonal marine field station dedicated to undergraduate education and research on 95 acre (0.4&nbsp;km&sup2;) <a href="/wiki/Appledore_Island" title="Appledore Island">Appledore Island</a> off the <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>–<a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> coast.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg/220px-Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg/330px-Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg/440px-Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_War_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A 
        <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> Memorial on Cornell's 
        <a href="/wiki/Cornell_West_Campus" title="Cornell West Campus">West Campus</a> in Ithaca
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Many Cornell facilities focus on <a href="/wiki/Conservationism" title="Conservationism" class="mw-redirect">conservationism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a>. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Agricultural_Experiment_Station" title="New York State Agricultural Experiment Station">New York State Agricultural Experiment Station</a>, operated by the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Agriculture_and_Life_Sciences" title="Cornell University College of Agriculture and Life Sciences">College of Agriculture and Life Sciences</a>, is in <a href="/wiki/Geneva,_New_York" title="Geneva, New York">Geneva, New York</a>, 50&nbsp;miles (80&nbsp;km) northwest of the main campus. The facility comprises 20 major buildings on 130&nbsp;acres (0.5&nbsp;km&sup2;) of land as well as more than 700&nbsp;acres (2.8&nbsp;km&sup2;) of test plots and other lands devoted to horticultural research.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> It also operates three substations: The Cornell Lake Erie Research and Extension Laboratory (CLEREL) in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_New_York" title="Portland, New York">Portland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Hudson Valley Laboratory in <a href="/wiki/Highland,_Ulster_County,_New_York" title="Highland, Ulster County, New York">Highland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Long Island Horticultural Research Laboratory in <a href="/wiki/Riverhead_(town),_New_York" title="Riverhead (town), New York">Riverhead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Artmuseum22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Artmuseum22.jpg/220px-Artmuseum22.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Artmuseum22.jpg/330px-Artmuseum22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Artmuseum22.jpg/440px-Artmuseum22.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Artmuseum22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Cornell's 
        <a href="/wiki/Herbert_F._Johnson_Museum_of_Art" title="Herbert F. Johnson Museum of Art">Herbert F. Johnson Museum of Art</a>, designed by 
        <a href="/wiki/I._M._Pei" title="I. M. Pei">I.M. Pei</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Lab_of_Ornithology" title="Cornell Lab of Ornithology">Cornell Lab of Ornithology</a> in Ithaca's Sapsucker Woods performs research on <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a>, primarily in birds.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> On April&nbsp;18, 2005, the lab announced that it had rediscovered the <a href="/wiki/Ivory-billed_Woodpecker" title="Ivory-billed Woodpecker">Ivory-billed Woodpecker</a>, long thought to be <a href="/wiki/Extinct" title="Extinct" class="mw-redirect">extinct</a> (Although some experts disputed the evidence and subsequent surveys were inconclusive).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The Animal Science Teaching and Research Center in <a href="/wiki/Harford,_New_York" title="Harford, New York">Harford, New York</a>, and the Duck Research Laboratory in <a href="/wiki/Eastport,_New_York" title="Eastport, New York">Eastport, New York</a>, are resources for information on animal disease control and <a href="/wiki/Husbandry" title="Husbandry" class="mw-redirect">husbandry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The Arnot Teaching and Research Forest, a 4,075 acre (16.5&nbsp;km&sup2;) forest 20&nbsp;miles (32.2&nbsp;km) south of the Ithaca campus, is the primary field location for faculty and student training and research related to professional <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> The mission of the Cornell Biological Field Station in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_New_York" title="Bridgeport, New York">Bridgeport, New York</a>, is &quot;to provide a center for long-term ecological research and support the University's educational programs, with special emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater" class="mw-redirect">freshwater</a> <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lacustrine</a> systems&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The Department of Horticulture operates the Homer C. Thompson Vegetable Research Farm and Freeville Organic Research Farm in <a href="/wiki/Freeville,_New_York" title="Freeville, New York">Freeville, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the university operates biodiversity laboratories in <a href="/wiki/Punta_Cana" title="Punta Cana">Punta Cana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> and in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" title="Amazon Rainforest" class="mw-redirect">Amazon Rainforest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> named the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Esbaran_Amazon_Field_Laboratory" title="Cornell University Esbaran Amazon Field Laboratory" class="mw-redirect">Cornell University Esbaran Amazon Field Laboratory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also maintains offices for <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">study abroad</a> and scholarship programs. The Cornell in Washington is a program that allows students to study for a semester in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, holding research and <a href="/wiki/Internship" title="Internship">internship</a> positions while earning <a href="/wiki/Credit_(education)" title="Credit (education)" class="mw-redirect">credit</a> toward a degree.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, operated by the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Architecture,_Art,_and_Planning" title="Cornell University College of Architecture, Art, and Planning">College of Architecture, Art, and Planning</a>, allows students to use the city as a resource for learning <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urban_studies" title="Urban studies" class="mw-redirect">urban studies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Human_Ecology" title="Cornell University College of Human Ecology">College of Human Ecology</a> offers the Urban Semester Program, an opportunity to take courses and complete an internship in New York City for a semester. As well, the Capital Semester program allows students to intern in the New York state legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> As <a href="/wiki/New_York_State" title="New York State" class="mw-redirect">New York State</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Land_grant" title="Land grant">land grant</a> college, Cornell operates a <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_extension_service" title="Cooperative extension service" class="mw-redirect">cooperative extension service</a> with 56 offices spread out across the state, each staffed with extension educators who offer programs in five subjects: Agriculture &amp; Food Systems; Children, Youth, &amp; Families; Community &amp; Economic Vitality; Environment &amp; Natural Resources; and Nutrition &amp; Health.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell also operates New York's Animal Health Diagnostic Center.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; font-size:90%; line-height:1.4em; width:280px;">

     <p>Cornell is a non-profit organization governed by a 64-member <a href="/wiki/Board_of_trustees" title="Board of trustees" class="mw-redirect">board of trustees</a> consisting of both privately and publicly appointed trustees. Three trustees are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a>; one seat is reserved for the eldest lineal descendant of Ezra Cornell; two members from each of the fields of agriculture, business and labor in New York state; eight trustees to be elected from among and by the alumni of the university; two trustees to be elected from among and by the faculty of the university at Ithaca and Geneva; two trustees to be elected from among and by the membership of the university's student body at Ithaca (one undergraduate and one graduate student);<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> and one trustee to be elected from among and by the nonacademic staff and employees of the university at Ithaca and Geneva, 37&nbsp;trustees at large and finally, the Governor, <a href="/wiki/Majority_Leader_of_the_New_York_State_Senate" title="Majority Leader of the New York State Senate">Temporary President of the Senate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_New_York_State_Assembly" title="Speaker of the New York State Assembly">Speaker of the Assembly</a>, and president of the university serve in an <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio" class="mw-redirect">ex officio</a></i> voting capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Bylaws_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bylaws-79"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_C._Meinig" title="Peter C. Meinig">Peter C. Meinig</a> has served as the chairman of the board since 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board elects a President to serve as the chief executive and educational officer.<sup id="cite_ref-Bylaws_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bylaws-79"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The twelfth and current president, <a href="/wiki/David_J._Skorton" title="David J. Skorton">David J. Skorton</a> has served since July 2006 and succeeded <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_S._Lehman" title="Jeffrey S. Lehman">Jeffrey S. Lehman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board of Trustees hold four regular meetings each year, and portions of those meetings are subject to the <a href="/wiki/Open_Meeting_Law" title="Open Meeting Law" class="mw-redirect">New York State Open Meetings Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell consists of nine privately endowed colleges as well as four publicly supported &quot;<a href="/wiki/Statutory_college" title="Statutory college">statutory colleges</a>&quot;: the New York State College of Agriculture and Life Sciences, College of Human Ecology, School of Industrial and Labor Relations, and College of Veterinary Medicine. These statutory colleges received $131.9&nbsp;million in <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">SUNY</a> appropriations in 2010-2011 to support their teaching, research, and service missions, which makes them accountable to SUNY trustees and other state agencies. The budget also includes $3.9 million of state funds for Cornell Cooperative Extension<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramanujan_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramanujan-85"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Graffeo_2005_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graffeo_2005-86"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Residents of New York enrolled in these colleges also qualify for discounted tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Attorney_General" title="New York State Attorney General" class="mw-redirect">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Eliot_Spitzer" title="Eliot Spitzer">Eliot Spitzer</a> issued a 2005 opinion asserting that, with respect to their academic activities, statutory colleges should be understood to be private, non-state parties.<sup id="cite_ref-Spitzer_2005_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spitzer_2005-7"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup>:1</sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell is <a href="/wiki/Decentralized" title="Decentralized" class="mw-redirect">decentralized</a>, with its colleges and schools exercising wide autonomy. Each defines its own academic programs, operates its own <a href="/wiki/College_admissions" title="College admissions" class="mw-redirect">admissions</a> and advising programs, and confers its own <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degrees</a>. The only university-wide requirements for a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">baccalaureate</a> degree are to pass a <a href="/wiki/Human_swimming" title="Human swimming">swimming</a> test, take two <a href="/wiki/Physical_education" title="Physical education">physical education</a> courses, and satisfy a writing requirement.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> A handful of inter-school academic departments offer courses in more than one college.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> All academic departments are affiliated with at least one college; the last department without such an affiliation, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Africana_Studies_and_Research_Center" title="Cornell Africana Studies and Research Center">Cornell Africana Studies and Research Center</a>, merged with the Arts College in July 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Seven schools provide undergraduate programs and an additional seven provide graduate and professional programs. Students pursuing graduate degrees in departments of these schools are enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Graduate_School" title="Cornell University Graduate School">Graduate School</a>. The School of Continuing Education and Summer Sessions offers programs for college and high school students, professionals, and other adults.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Of the 13,515 undergraduate students, 4,251 (31.5%) are affiliated with the largest college by enrollment, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Cornell University College of Arts and Sciences">Arts and Sciences</a>, followed by 3,153 (23.3%) in <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Agriculture_and_Life_Sciences" title="Cornell University College of Agriculture and Life Sciences">Agriculture and Life Sciences</a> and 2,680 (19.8%) in <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Engineering" title="Cornell University College of Engineering">Engineering</a>. By student enrollment, the smallest of the seven undergraduate colleges is <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Architecture,_Art,_and_Planning" title="Cornell University College of Architecture, Art, and Planning">Architecture, Art, and Planning</a>, with 515 (3.8%) students.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several other universities have used Cornell as their model, including <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sydney" title="University of Sydney">University of Sydney</a> in Australia, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">University of Birmingham</a> in the United Kingdom; the latter on the recommendation of one of its financiers, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a>, who was a Cornell Trustee.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also operates <a href="/wiki/ECornell" title="ECornell">eCornell</a>, which offers both certificate programs and professional development courses online.<sup id="cite_ref-About_eCornell_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_eCornell-94"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to being New York's land-grant college, Cornell is also is a partner in New York's sea-grant program,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> is the hub of the Northeast's sun-grant program,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> and is a part of New York's space-grant consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2009, Cornell ranked third among universities in the U.S. in fund-raising, collecting <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>446.75&nbsp;million in private support.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to the central University development staff located in Ithaca and New York City, each college and program has its own staffed fundraising program. In 2006, Cornell launched a $4&nbsp;billion fundraising campaign, which reached $3&nbsp;billion in November&nbsp;2010.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:SageHallexterior.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/SageHallexterior.JPG/170px-SageHallexterior.JPG" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/SageHallexterior.JPG/255px-SageHallexterior.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/SageHallexterior.JPG/340px-SageHallexterior.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:SageHallexterior.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Sage_Hall" title="Sage Hall">Sage Hall</a>, home to the 
        <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Curtis_Johnson_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management">Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell is a large, primarily residential research university with a majority of enrollments in undergraduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-100"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has been <a href="/wiki/Accreditation" title="Accreditation">accredited</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Middle_States_Commission_on_Higher_Education" title="Middle States Commission on Higher Education" class="mw-redirect">Middle States Commission on Higher Education</a> since 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell operates on a 4–1–4 academic calendar with the fall term beginning in late August and ending in early December, a three-week winter session in January, and the spring term beginning in late January and ending in early May.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university awarded the world's first degree in <a href="/wiki/Journalism" title="Journalism">journalism</a>, the nation's first university degree in <a href="/wiki/Veterinary_medicine" title="Veterinary medicine">veterinary medicine</a>, and the first doctorates in <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_engineering" title="Industrial engineering">industrial engineering</a>. It also established the first four-year schools of hotel administration and industrial and labor relations. Cornell was the first U.S. university to offer a major in American studies, and it was the first university to teach modern Far Eastern languages.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell and <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_University" title="Oregon State University">Oregon State University</a> are the only two institutions which are members of the <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">Land Grant</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Sea_Grant_College_Program" title="National Sea Grant College Program">Sea Grant</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Grant_College_and_Fellowship_Program" title="National Space Grant College and Fellowship Program">Space Grant</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sun_grant_colleges" title="Sun grant colleges">Sun Grant</a> programs.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>For the undergraduate class of 2017, Cornell admitted a total of 6,062 students out of 40,006 applicants, for an acceptance rate of 15.15%.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell's College of Arts and Sciences admitted less than 14% of applicants for the class of 2015. For the students enrolling in the class of 2016, 91% were in the top 10% of their class.<sup id="cite_ref-EnteringClassProfile_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnteringClassProfile-104"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> For the undergraduate class of 2013, the admission rate was 19.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-CornellAdmissions_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CornellAdmissions-105"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> For the undergraduate class of 2012, the admission rate was 20.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Of those admitted, the average <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> Verbal score was 700, while the average SAT Math was a 720. Also, 92% of admitted students for the Class of 2011 were in the top 10% of their graduating high school class.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell's policy of requiring students to submit all their SAT scores is uncommon among American universities.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell enrolls students from all 50 U.S. states and more than 120 countries. The Class of 2010 has representatives from all states. As of Fall 2005, 28% of undergraduate students identified themselves as members of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minority groups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Legacy applicants receive a slight advantage in the admission process.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Graduate_School" title="Cornell University Graduate School">Graduate School</a> accepted 21.6% of applicants, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Law_School" title="Cornell Law School">Law School</a> accepted 20.6%, and the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Veterinary_Medicine" title="Cornell University College of Veterinary Medicine">Veterinary School</a> accepted 10.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Weill_Medical_College_of_Cornell_University" title="Weill Medical College of Cornell University" class="mw-redirect">Weill Cornell Medical School</a> accepted 4.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2010)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Curtis_Johnson_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management">Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management</a> accepted 28% of its applicants for its two-year MBA program.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_aid">Financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Financial aid">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus,_Sage_Chapel,_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus%2C_Sage_Chapel%2C_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg/220px-Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus%2C_Sage_Chapel%2C_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus%2C_Sage_Chapel%2C_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg/330px-Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus%2C_Sage_Chapel%2C_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus%2C_Sage_Chapel%2C_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg/440px-Jennie_McGraw_sarcophagus%2C_Sage_Chapel%2C_Cornell_Univ_Ithaca_NY.jpg 2x" /></a>

        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Sarcophagus" title="Sarcophagus">sarcophagus</a> in

        <a href="/wiki/Jennie_McGraw" title="Jennie McGraw">Jennie McGraw</a>, Cornell

       </div>
