     <p>At the time of its founding, Cornell University was considered revolutionary because its founder, Ezra Cornell, was committed to access for all students, regardless of economic circumstance. Section 9 of the original charter of Cornell University ensured that the university &quot;shall be open to applicants for admission&nbsp;... at the lowest rates of expense consistent with its welfare and efficiency, and without distinction as to rank, class, previous occupation or locality.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-charter_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-115"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The University Charter provided for free instruction to one student chosen from each Assembly district in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-115"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Within the first 10 years of operation, the university admitted women and underrepresented minority students and provided financial aid for many students, using a combination of grant, loan and work-study opportunities. The university awarded need-based grants as early as 1879, and its first endowed scholarship fund was created in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Starting in the 1950s Cornell coordinated with other Ivy League schools to provide a consistent set of financial aid. However, in 1989, a consent decree to end a Justice Department antitrust investigation ended such coordination.<sup id="cite_ref-2005-06_Financial_Plan_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005-06_Financial_Plan-117"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Even after the decree, all Ivy League schools continue to award aid on financial need without offering any athletic scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2010, Cornell announced a policy of matching any grant component of financial aid offers from other Ivy League schools, MIT, Duke University or Stanford, if an accepted applicant is trying to decide between Cornell and those other schools.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On January 31, 2008, Cornell announced a new financial aid initiative to be phased in over the following two years. In the first year, 2008–09, Cornell replaced need-based loans with scholarships for undergraduate students from families with incomes under $60,000 and capped such loans annually at $3,000 for students from families with incomes between $60,000 and $120,000. The following year, 2009–10, the program improved by replacing loan with scholarships for students from families with incomes up to $75,000, and capped annual loans at $3,000 for students from families with income between $75,000 and $120,000. For families above $120,000, need-based loans were capped at $7,500 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The initiative costs an additional $14&nbsp;million per year to fully implement.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Cornell's endowment dropped 27% in the second half of 2008, its President announced that the financial aid initiative will continue by withdrawing an additional $35&nbsp;million from the endowment for undergraduate financial aid in 2009–10.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell is seeking $125&nbsp;million in gifts to support the financial aid initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, 1,647 of the 3,181 full-time freshmen enrolled were found to have financial need (40%).<sup id="cite_ref-fa_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fa-124"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Of these, Cornell could meet the full financial aid needs of all 1,647 freshmen. Cornell's average undergraduate student's indebtedness at graduation is $21,549.<sup id="cite_ref-fa_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fa-124"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_programs">International programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Bhangra.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bhangra.JPG/220px-Bhangra.JPG" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bhangra.JPG/330px-Bhangra.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/Bhangra.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Bhangra.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Students performing a 
        <a href="/wiki/Dandiya_Raas" title="Dandiya Raas">Raas</a>, a traditional folk dance from 
        <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell offers undergraduate curricula with international focuses, including the <a href="/wiki/African_Studies" title="African Studies" class="mw-redirect">Africana Studies</a>, French Studies, German Studies, <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Studies" title="Jewish Studies" class="mw-redirect">Jewish Studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latino_studies" title="Latino studies">Latino Studies</a>, Near Eastern Studies, <a href="/wiki/Romance_studies" title="Romance studies">Romance Studies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Literature" title="Russian Literature" class="mw-redirect">Russian Literature</a> majors. Cornell was the first university to teach modern Far Eastern languages.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to traditional academic programs, Cornell students may study abroad on any of six continents.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Studies" title="Asian Studies" class="mw-redirect">Asian Studies</a> major, <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South Asia Program (page does not exist)">South Asia Program</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_South_East_Asia_Program" title="Cornell South East Asia Program" class="mw-redirect">South East Asia Program</a> and China and Asia-Pacific Studies (CAPS) major provide opportunities for students and researchers in Asia. Cornell has an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a> allowing students in the CAPS major to spend a semester in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Engineering" title="Cornell University College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a> has an agreement to exchange faculty and graduate students with <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_School_of_Hotel_Administration" title="Cornell University School of Hotel Administration">School of Hotel Administration</a> has a joint master's program with <a href="/wiki/Nanyang_Technological_University" title="Nanyang Technological University">Nanyang Technological University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Agriculture_and_Life_Sciences" title="Cornell University College of Agriculture and Life Sciences">College of Agriculture and Life Sciences</a> has signed an agreement with Japan's National Institute of Agrobiological Sciences,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines,_Los_Ba%C3%B1os" title="University of the Philippines, Los Ba&ntilde;os" class="mw-redirect">University of the Philippines, Los Ba&ntilde;os</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> to engage in joint research and exchange graduate students and faculty members. It also cooperates in agricultural research with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Council_of_Agricultural_Research" title="Indian Council of Agricultural Research">Indian Council of Agricultural Research</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell also offers a course on International consulting in association with <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Bangalore" title="Indian Institute of Management Bangalore">Indian Institute of Management Bangalore</a><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, Cornell's efforts focus on biology and medicine. The <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College_in_Qatar" title="Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar">Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar</a> trains new doctors to improve health services in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is also developing the Bridging the Rift Center, a &quot;Library of Life&quot; (or <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> of all living systems) on the border of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, in collaboration with those two countries and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell has partnered with <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a> in Canada to offer a joint <a href="/wiki/Executive_MBA" title="Executive MBA" class="mw-redirect">Executive MBA</a>. The innovative program includes both on-campus and <a href="/wiki/Videoconferencing" title="Videoconferencing">videoconferencing</a>-based, interactive virtual classroom sessions. Graduates of the program earn both a Cornell MBA and a Queen's MBA.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell University is member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Academic_Impact" title="United Nations Academic Impact">United Nations Academic Impact</a> aligning institutions of higher education to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and promoting international cooperation.</p>

     <p>In 2012, Cornell ranked 14th in the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> and 16th in the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings-142"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> (in 2010 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> and <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> parted ways to produce separate rankings). The university ranked 15th in the 2011 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> National Universities ranking (tied with <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a>), tied for 6th with <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a> in the 2011 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> High School Counselor rankings, and 13th globally in an academic ranking of world universities by <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell was ranked 38th nationally and sixth among <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> universities in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Monthly" title="The Washington Monthly" class="mw-redirect">The Washington Monthly</a>'</i>s 2010 ranking of universities' contributions to research, community service, and <a href="/wiki/Social_mobility" title="Social mobility">social mobility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> reported that Cornell ranked ninth as a &quot;dream college&quot; for high school students and their parents,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> however the school is not featured in the 2011 top ten list. <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> named Cornell the 'Hottest Ivy' in its 2007 listing of America's 25 Hot Schools.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Instead of using the traditional school ranking methods, <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> offers a snapshot of today's most interesting colleges according to high school counselors, admissions officers, consultants, students, and parents, who noted Cornell for its emphasis on &quot;problem-solving as well as scholarly debate&quot; and &quot;variety on campus&quot; among other things.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell ranked 14th among 300 Best World Universities in 2011 compiled by <a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a> (HRLR) on Measurements of World's Top 300 Universities Graduates' Performance .<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Forbes</i> ranked Cornell 51st in 2011, based on student criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In its annual edition of &quot;America's Best Architecture &amp; Design Schools&quot;, the journal <i>DesignIntelligence</i> has consistently ranked Cornell's Bachelor of Architecture program as number one in the nation (2000–2002, 2005–2007, and 2009–2011). In the 2011 survey, the program ranked first and the Master of Architecture program ranked sixth.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011 and 2012, Design Intelligence ranked Cornell's Master of Landscape Architecture program 4th in the nation with the undergraduate program placing 8th for the same two years.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, US News and World Report ranked Cornell's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.human.cornell.edu/pam/sloan/index.cfm">Sloan Program in Health Administration</a> 14th in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">

        <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> ceremony at 
        <a href="/wiki/Schoellkopf_Field" title="Schoellkopf Field">Schoellkopf Field</a>
       </div>

     <p>Among business schools in the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Charles_H._Dyson_School_of_Applied_Economics_and_Management" title="Charles H. Dyson School of Applied Economics and Management">Charles H. Dyson School of Applied Economics and Management</a> (Cornell's <a href="/wiki/AACSB" title="AACSB" class="mw-redirect">AACSB</a>-accredited undergraduate business school) was ranked 3rd by <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> and 10th by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> <sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> in 2012. The <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Curtis_Johnson_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management">Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management</a> was ranked 7th by <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a></i> in 2012, 9th by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> 14th by <i>U.S. News</i> in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> and 18th by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Worldwide, the school was ranked 17th by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in 2005 and 36th by the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>U.S. News</i> ranked the <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_School" title="Weill Cornell Medical School" class="mw-redirect">Weill Cornell Medical School</a> as the 15th best in the United States in its 2007 edition.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Veterinary_Medicine" title="Cornell University College of Veterinary Medicine">College of Veterinary Medicine</a> is ranked first among national veterinary medical schools.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Law_School" title="Cornell Law School">Cornell Law School</a> was ranked as the 12th best graduate law program among national universities.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, <i><a href="/wiki/The_National_Law_Journal" title="The National Law Journal">The National Law Journal</a></i> reported that Cornell Law had the sixth highest placement rate at the top 50 law firms in the U.S. among law schools with recent graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Among graduate engineering programs, Cornell was ranked 9th in the United States by <i>U.S. News</i> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, Cornell was ranked 1st in the United States and 4th in the world in producing the most graduates who went on to receive engineering or natural science Ph.D.'s at American universities.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> In its 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> and 2008<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> ranking of undergraduate engineering programs at universities in the United States, <i>U.S. News</i> placed Cornell 1st in <a href="/wiki/Engineering_physics" title="Engineering physics">engineering physics</a>. In 1954, <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Hilton" title="Conrad Hilton">Conrad Hilton</a> called the Cornell <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_School_of_Hotel_Administration" title="Cornell University School of Hotel Administration">School of Hotel Administration</a> &quot;the greatest hotel school in the world.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the latest ranking of <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" title="United States National Research Council">National Research Council</a> in 1995, Cornell ranks sixth nationally in the number of graduate programs in the top ten in their fields.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell had 19 ranked in the top 10 in terms of overall academic quality. Also <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" title="United States National Research Council">National Research Council</a> ranked the quality of faculties as 5th in Arts and Humanities, 6th in Mathematics and Physical Sciences, and 5th in Engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell's <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> offerings are also ranked in <i><a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy_(magazine)" title="Foreign Policy (magazine)" class="mw-redirect">Foreign Policy</a></i> magazine's <a href="/wiki/Inside_the_Ivory_Tower" title="Inside the Ivory Tower">Inside the Ivory Tower</a> survey, which lists the world's top twenty of such programs at the undergraduate, Master's and Ph.D. levels.<sup id="cite_ref-ivorytower2012_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ivorytower2012-176"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, the survey ranked Cornell 11th overall for doctoral programs and 12th overall in the undergraduate category.<sup id="cite_ref-tripsurvey_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tripsurvey-177"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library">Library</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Library">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG/170px-Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG/255px-Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG/340px-Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_Law_School_Library.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Law_School#Library" title="Cornell Law School">Cornell Law Library</a> is one of 12 national depositories for print records of briefs filed with the 
        <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Supreme Court</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Library" title="Cornell University Library">Cornell University Library</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Cornell University Library is the 11th largest academic library in the United States, ranked by number of <a href="/wiki/Book#Collections_of_books" title="Book">volumes</a> held.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> Organized into 20 divisions, in 2005 it held 7.5&nbsp;million printed volumes in open stacks, 8.2&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Microfilm" title="Microfilm" class="mw-redirect">microfilms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microfiche" title="Microfiche" class="mw-redirect">microfiches</a>, and a total of 440,000 maps, motion pictures, DVDs, sound recordings, and computer files in its collections, in addition to extensive digital resources and the University Archives.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> It was the first among all U.S. colleges and universities to allow <a href="/wiki/Undergraduates" title="Undergraduates" class="mw-redirect">undergraduates</a> to borrow books from its libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> ranked it as the 11th best college library,<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_2006_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton_2006-180"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> and it climbed to 6th best in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_2009_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton_2009-181"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> The library plays an active role in furthering online archiving of scientific and historical documents. <a href="/wiki/ArXiv" title="ArXiv">arXiv</a>, an <a href="/wiki/E-print" title="E-print" class="mw-redirect">e-print</a> archive created at <a href="/wiki/Los_Alamos_National_Laboratory" title="Los Alamos National Laboratory">Los Alamos National Laboratory</a> by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ginsparg" title="Paul Ginsparg">Paul Ginsparg</a>, is operated and primarily funded by Cornell as part of the library's services. The archive has changed the way many <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mathematician" title="Mathematician">mathematicians</a> communicate, making the e-print a viable and popular means of announcing new research.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press_and_scholarly_publications">Press and scholarly publications</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Press and scholarly publications">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Press" title="Cornell University Press">Cornell University Press</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Cornell University Press, established in 1869 but inactive from 1884 to 1930, was the first university <a href="/wiki/Publishing" title="Publishing">publishing</a> enterprise in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Bishop1962_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bishop1962-183"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-press_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press-184"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> Today, the press is one of the country's largest <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press" class="mw-redirect">university presses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> It produces approximately 150 nonfiction titles each year in various disciplines including anthropology, Asian studies, biological sciences, classics, history, industrial relations, literary criticism and theory, natural history, philosophy, politics and international relations, veterinary science, and women's studies.<sup id="cite_ref-press_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press-184"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell's academic units and student groups also publish a number of scholarly journals. Faculty-led publications include the Johnson School's <i><a href="/wiki/Administrative_Science_Quarterly" title="Administrative Science Quarterly">Administrative Science Quarterly</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> the ILR School's <i><a href="/wiki/Industrial_and_Labor_Relations_Review" title="Industrial and Labor Relations Review">Industrial and Labor Relations Review</a></i>, the Arts and Sciences Philosophy Department's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philosophical_Review" title="The Philosophical Review">The Philosophical Review</a></i>, the College of Architecture, Art, and Planning's <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_Journal_of_Architecture" title="Cornell Journal of Architecture">Journal of Architecture</a></i>, and the Law School's <i><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Empirical_Legal_Studies" title="Journal of Empirical Legal Studies">Journal of Empirical Legal Studies</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> Student-led scholarly publications include the <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_Law_Review" title="Cornell Law Review">Law Review</a></i>, the Public Affairs School's Cornell Policy Review, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_International_Law_Journal" title="Cornell International Law Journal">International Law Journal</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_Journal_of_Law_and_Public_Policy" title="Cornell Journal of Law and Public Policy">Journal of Law and Public Policy</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_International_Affairs_Review" title="Cornell International Affairs Review">International Affairs Review</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_HR_Review" title="Cornell HR Review">HR Review</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Physical_Review" title="Physical Review">Physical Review</a>, recognized internationally as among the best and well known journals of physics, was founded at Cornell in 1893 before being later managed by the <a href="/wiki/American_Physical_Society" title="American Physical Society">American Physical Society</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Decentrhodeshall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Decentrhodeshall.jpg/220px-Decentrhodeshall.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Decentrhodeshall.jpg/330px-Decentrhodeshall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/92/Decentrhodeshall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Decentrhodeshall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Cornell's 
        <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Center_for_Advanced_Computing" title="Cornell University Center for Advanced Computing">Center for Advanced Computing</a> was one of the five original centers of the 
        <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">NSF's</a> Supercomputer Centers Program.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg/220px-Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg/330px-Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg/440px-Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_Plantations_lake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Plantations" title="Cornell Plantations">Cornell Plantations</a>, located adjacent to the Ithaca campus, is used for 
        <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation research</a> as well as for recreation by Cornellians
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg/220px-Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg/330px-Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg/440px-Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Dickson_White_statue_and_Goldwin_Smith_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> In the basement of 
        <a href="/wiki/Goldwin_Smith" title="Goldwin Smith">Goldwin Smith</a> Hall, researchers in the 
        <a href="/wiki/Dendrochronology" title="Dendrochronology">Dendrochronology</a> Lab determine the age of archaeological artifacts found at digs
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell, a research university, is ranked fourth in the world in producing the largest number of graduates who go on to pursue PhDs in <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural sciences</a> at American institutions, as well as fifth in the world in producing graduates who pursue PhDs at American institutions in any field.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> Research is a central element of the university's mission; in 2009 Cornell spent <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>671&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Million" title="Million">million</a> on science and engineering research and development, the 16th highest in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For the 2004–05 fiscal year, the university spent $561.3&nbsp;million on research.<sup id="cite_ref-research_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-research-190"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> The primary recipients of this funding were the colleges of Medicine ($164.2&nbsp;million), Agriculture and Life Sciences ($114.5&nbsp;million), Arts and Sciences ($80.3&nbsp;million), and Engineering ($64.8&nbsp;million).<sup id="cite_ref-research_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-research-190"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> The money comes largely from federal sources, with federal investment of $381.0&nbsp;million. The federal agencies that invest the most money are the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="Department of Health and Human Services" class="mw-redirect">Department of Health and Human Services</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> that make up, respectively, 51.4% and 30.7% of all federal investment in the university.<sup id="cite_ref-research_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-research-190"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell was on the top-ten list of U.S. universities receiving the most <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> in 2003, and was one of the nation's top five institutions in forming <a href="/wiki/Start-up_companies" title="Start-up companies" class="mw-redirect">start-up companies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004–05, Cornell received 200 invention disclosures, filed 203 U.S. patent applications, completed 77 commercial license agreements, and distributed <a href="/wiki/Royalties" title="Royalties">royalties</a> of more than $4.1&nbsp;million to Cornell units and inventors.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 1962, Cornell has been involved in unmanned missions to <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 21st century, Cornell had a hand in the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover" title="Mars Exploration Rover">Mars Exploration Rover Mission</a>. Cornell's <a href="/wiki/Steve_Squyres" title="Steve Squyres">Steve Squyres</a>, Principal Investigator for the Athena Science Payload, led the selection of the landing zones and requested data collection features for the <a href="/wiki/Spirit_rover" title="Spirit rover" class="mw-redirect">Spirit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_rover" title="Opportunity rover" class="mw-redirect">Opportunity rovers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> engineers took those requests and designed the rovers to meet them. The rovers, both of which have operated long past their original life expectancies, are responsible for the discoveries that were awarded 2004 Breakthrough of the Year honors by <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> Control of the Mars rovers has shifted between NASA's Jet Propulsion Laboratory at <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">Caltech</a> and Cornell's Space Sciences Building.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> Further, Cornell researchers discovered the <a href="/wiki/Rings_of_Uranus" title="Rings of Uranus">rings</a> around the planet <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> and Cornell built and operated the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory" title="Arecibo Observatory">world's largest and most sensitive radiotelescope</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> until 2011, when they transferred the operations to <a href="/wiki/SRI_International" title="SRI International">SRI International</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Universities_Space_Research_Association" title="Universities Space Research Association">Universities Space Research Association</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_University_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Metropolitan University (Puerto Rico)">Metropolitan University of Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Automotive_Crash_Injury_Research_Project" title="Automotive Crash Injury Research Project" class="mw-redirect">Automotive Crash Injury Research Project</a> was begun in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-cars_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cars-198"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> It pioneered the use of <a href="/wiki/Crash_test" title="Crash test">crash testing</a>, originally using corpses rather than <a href="/wiki/Crash_test_dummy" title="Crash test dummy">dummies</a>. The project discovered that improved door locks, energy-absorbing steering wheels, padded dashboards, and seat belts could prevent an extraordinary percentage of injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-cars_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cars-198"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the early 1980s, Cornell deployed the first IBM 3090-400VF and coupled two IBM 3090-600E systems to investigate course-grained parallel computing. In 1984, the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> began work on establishing five new <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">supercomputer</a> centers, including the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Theory_Center" title="Cornell Theory Center" class="mw-redirect">Cornell Center for Advanced Computing</a>, to provide high-speed computing resources for research within the United States. As an NSF center, Cornell deployed the first IBM Scalable Parallel supercomputer. In the 1990s, Cornell developed scheduling software and deployed the first supercomputer built by Dell. Most recently, Cornell deployed Red Cloud, one of the first cloud computing services designed specifically for research. Today, the center is a partner on the National Science Foundation XSEDE supercomputing program, providing coordination for XSEDE architecture and design, systems reliability testing, and online training using the Cornell Virtual Workshop learning platform.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell scientists have researched the fundamental particles of nature for more than 70 years. Cornell physicists, such as <a href="/wiki/Hans_Bethe" title="Hans Bethe">Hans Bethe</a>, contributed not only to the foundations of nuclear physics but also participated in the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a> (see also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cornell_Manhattan_Project_people" title="List of Cornell Manhattan Project people">List of Cornell Manhattan Project people</a>). In the 1930s, Cornell built the second <a href="/wiki/Cyclotron" title="Cyclotron">cyclotron</a> in the United States. In the 1950s, Cornell physicists became the first to study <a href="/wiki/Synchrotron_radiation" title="Synchrotron radiation">synchrotron radiation</a>. During the 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_High_Energy_Synchrotron_Source" title="Cornell High Energy Synchrotron Source" class="mw-redirect">Cornell Electron Storage Ring</a>, located beneath Alumni Field, was the world's highest-luminosity electron-positron collider.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> After building the synchrotron at Cornell, <a href="/wiki/Robert_R._Wilson" title="Robert R. Wilson">Robert R. Wilson</a> took a leave of absence to become the founding director of <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a>, which involved designing and building the largest accelerator in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell's accelerator and high-energy physics groups are involved in the design of the proposed <a href="/wiki/International_Linear_Collider" title="International Linear Collider">International Linear Collider</a> and plan to participate in its construction and operation. The International Linear Collider, to be completed in the late 2010s, will complement the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a> and shed light on questions such as the identity of <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">dark matter</a> and the existence of extra dimensions.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the area of humanities and social sciences, Cornell is best known for being one of the world's greatest centers for the study of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_South_East_Asia_Program" title="Cornell South East Asia Program" class="mw-redirect">Southeast Asia Program</a> (SEAP) at Cornell is designated as a <a href="/wiki/National_Resource_Center" title="National Resource Center">National Resource Center</a> (NRC) by the United States Department of Education 2010–2014. Therefore, the SEAP is nationally prominent in promoting advanced foreign language training, area and international knowledge in the liberal arts and applied discipline focused on Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.einaudi.cornell.edu/southeastasia/resources/research.asp">George McTurnan Kahin Center for Advanced Research on Southeast Asia</a> is located in the historic &quot;Treman House.&quot; The house was built by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Henry_Treman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Robert Henry Treman (page does not exist)">Robert Henry Treman</a>, the son of an enterprising local family and the first member of that family to attend Cornell University and be elected to its board of trustees. The <a href="/wiki/George_McTurnan_Kahin" title="George McTurnan Kahin">George McTurnan Kahin</a> Center is home to SEAP graduate students, visiting fellows and scholars, faculty members, and SEAP's Publication and Outreach offices.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Q%26D.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Q%26D.jpg/170px-Q%26D.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Q%26D.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Q%26D.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Q%26D.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Lyon Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>For the 2006–07 academic year, Cornell had 901 registered student organizations. These clubs and organizations run the gamut from kayaking to full-armor jousting, from varsity and club sports and a cappella groups to improvisational theatre, from political clubs and publications to chess and video game clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> They are subsidized financially by academic departments and/or the Student Assembly and the Graduate &amp; Professional Student Assembly, two student-run organizations with a collective budget of $3.0&nbsp;million per year.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> The assemblies also finance other student life programs including a concert commission and an on-campus theater. The Cornell International Affairs Society sends over 100 Cornellians to collegiate Model United Nations conferences across North America and hosts the Cornell Model United Nations Conference each spring for over 500 high school students. Additionally, the Cornell International Affairs Society's travelling Model United Nations team is ranked number 16 in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_United_Religious_Work&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cornell United Religious Work (page does not exist)">Cornell United Religious Work</a> is a collaboration among many diverse religious traditions, helping to provide spiritual resources throughout a student's time at college. The <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Catholic_Community" title="Cornell Catholic Community">Cornell Catholic Community</a> is the largest Catholic student organization on campus, updated to Vatican II in 2004 by Mr. Jackson Browne. Mr. Browne, a quiet student of religious studies and known best for his relationship between the Provost and many Student organizations. Student organizations also include a myriad of musical groups that play everything from classical, jazz, to ethnic styles in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Big_Red_Marching_Band" title="Big Red Marching Band" class="mw-redirect">Big Red Marching Band</a>, which performs regularly at football games and other campus events.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> Organized in 1868, the oldest Cornell student organization is the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_Glee_Club" title="Cornell University Glee Club">Cornell University Glee Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is home to two <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_secret_societies_in_North_America" title="Collegiate secret societies in North America">secret honor societies</a> called <a href="/wiki/Sphinx_Head" title="Sphinx Head">Sphinx Head</a><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Quill_and_Dagger" title="Quill and Dagger">Quill and Dagger</a><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> that have maintained a presence on campus for well over 120 years. It also has a Student Innovation Group, a think-tank dedicated to improving student life on campus.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell hosts a large <a href="/wiki/List_of_fraternities_and_sororities_at_Cornell_University" title="List of fraternities and sororities at Cornell University">fraternity and sorority system</a>, with 70 chapters involving 33% of male and 24% of female undergraduates.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Greek_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-216"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">Alpha Phi Alpha</a>, the first intercollegiate <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">Greek-letter</a> organization established for <a href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African Americans</a>, was founded at Cornell in 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell's connection to national Greek life is strong and longstanding. The chapter house of <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a> constructed in 1877 was the first house built in America solely for fratnerity use.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 2004–05 academic year, the Greek system committed 21,668 <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a> and <a href="/wiki/Advocacy" title="Advocacy">advocacy</a> hours and raised $176,547 in philanthropic efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-Greek_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-216"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the administration has expressed concerns over student misconduct in the system.<sup id="cite_ref-Greek_216-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-216"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Misconduct by students, faculty or staff is reviewed by the Judicial Administrator, who administers Cornell's <a href="/wiki/Justice_system" title="Justice system" class="mw-redirect">justice system</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Press_and_radio">Press and radio</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Press and radio">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Cornell student body produces several works by way of print and radio. Student-run press outlets include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cornell_Daily_Sun" title="The Cornell Daily Sun">The Cornell Daily Sun</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cornell_Review" title="The Cornell Review">The Cornell Review</a></i>, the alternative to the daily with a foundation as a <a href="/wiki/American_conservatism" title="American conservatism" class="mw-redirect">conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspaper</a>.</p> 
     <p>Other press outlets include a campus humor magazine; the <i><a href="/wiki/Cornell_Chronicle" title="Cornell Chronicle">Cornell Chronicle</a></i>, the university's newspaper of record; and <i><a href="/wiki/Kitsch_(magazine)" title="Kitsch (magazine)">Kitsch Magazine</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Feature_story" title="Feature story">feature magazine</a> published in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Ithaca_College" title="Ithaca College">Ithaca College</a>. <i>The Cornellian</i> is an independent student organization that organizes, arranges, produces, edits, and publishes the yearbook of the same name; it is composed of artistic photos of the campus, student life, and athletics, as well as the standard senior portraits. It carries the Silver Crown Award for Journalism as well as a Benjamin Franklin Award for Print Design – the only Ivy League Yearbook with such a distinction.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornellians are represented over the radio waves on <a href="/wiki/WVBR" title="WVBR" class="mw-redirect">WVBR</a>, an independent commercial FM radio station owned and operated by Cornell students. Other student groups also operate internet streaming audio sites.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_footbridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cornell_footbridge.jpg/220px-Cornell_footbridge.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cornell_footbridge.jpg/330px-Cornell_footbridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cornell_footbridge.jpg/440px-Cornell_footbridge.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_footbridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> One of several 
        <a href="/wiki/Footbridge" title="Footbridge">footbridges</a> that span Cornell's 
        <a href="/wiki/Gorge" title="Gorge" class="mw-redirect">gorges</a> and ease commuting from housing to academic buildings on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>University housing is broadly divided into three sections: <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus" title="Cornell North Campus">North Campus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_West_Campus" title="Cornell West Campus">West Campus</a>, and Collegetown. Since a 1997 residential initiative, West Campus houses transfer and returning students, whereas North Campus is almost entirely populated by freshmen.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The only options for living on North Campus for upperclassmen are the program houses: <a href="/wiki/Risley_Residential_College" title="Risley Residential College">Risley Residential College</a>, Just About Music, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus#Ecology_House" title="Cornell North Campus">Ecology House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus#Holland_International_Living_Center" title="Cornell North Campus">Holland International Living Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus#Multicultural_Living_Learning_Unit" title="Cornell North Campus">Multicultural Living Learning Unit</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus#Latino_Living_Center" title="Cornell North Campus">Latino Living Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus#Akwe:kon" title="Cornell North Campus">Akwe:kon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cornell_North_Campus#Ujamaa" title="Cornell North Campus">Ujamaa</a>. In an attempt to create a sense of community and an atmosphere of education outside the classroom and continue Andrew Dickson White's vision, a $250&nbsp;million reconstruction of West Campus created <a href="/wiki/Cornell_West_Campus#House_system" title="Cornell West Campus">residential colleges</a> there for undergraduates.<sup id="cite_ref-houses_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houses-224"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> The idea of building a house system can be attributed in part to the success of Risley Residential College, the oldest continually operating residential college at Cornell.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Additionally, Cornell has several housing areas for graduate and professional students. Of these, Schuyler House (which was formerly a part of Sage Infirmary)<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> and Hughes Hall (which is the domitory wing of the law school complex)<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> have a dorm layout, while Maplewood Apartments, Hasbrouck Apartments, and Thurston Court Apartments are apartment-style, some even allowing for family living. Off campus, many single-family houses in the East Hill neighborhoods adjacent to the university have been converted to apartments. Private developers have also built several multi-story apartment complexes in the Collegetown neighborhood. Nine percent of undergraduate students reside in fraternity and sorority houses, although first semester freshmen are not permitted to join them.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell's Greek system has 67 chapters and over 54 Greek residences that house approximately 1,500 students. About 42% of Greek members live in their houses.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Housing_cooperative" title="Housing cooperative">Housing cooperatives</a> or other independent living units exist, including Watermargin, <a href="/wiki/Telluride_Association" title="Telluride Association">Telluride House</a>, Triphammer Cooperative, the Center for Jewish Living, the Wait Cooperative and most famously the ever-prestigious, Cayuga Lodge.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Cornell's dining system was ranked 11th in the nation by the <i>Princeton Review</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has 30 on-campus dining locations, and a program called the Cross Country Gourmet Guest Restaurant Series periodically brings chefs, menus, and atmosphere from restaurants to Cornell's ten cafeterias.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="width: 744px; margin: 0 auto;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div style="clear: both; font-weight: bold; text-align: center; background-color:">

       </div>

         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg/180px-Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg" width="180" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg/270px-Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg/360px-Cornell_West_campus_dormitories.jpg 2x" /></a>
