     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Big_Red" title="Cornell Big Red">Cornell Big Red</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_Baseball2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cornell_Baseball2.jpg/170px-Cornell_Baseball2.jpg" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cornell_Baseball2.jpg/255px-Cornell_Baseball2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cornell_Baseball2.jpg/340px-Cornell_Baseball2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell_Baseball2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A 1908 print depicting a Cornell 
        <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> player
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell has 36 varsity intercollegiate teams that have the nickname of the Big Red. An <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> institution, Cornell is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League#Athletics_.26_competition" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> and <a href="/wiki/ECAC_Hockey" title="ECAC Hockey">ECAC Hockey</a> and competes in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference" title="Eastern College Athletic Conference">Eastern College Athletic Conference</a> (ECAC), the largest athletic conference in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> (Note that ECAC Hockey is no longer affiliated with the ECAC.) Cornell's varsity athletic teams currently are highly successful within the Ivy League and consistently challenge for NCAA Division I titles in a number of sports, including <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Big_Red_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Cornell Big Red men's lacrosse">men's lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Big_Red_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Cornell Big Red men's ice hockey">men's ice hockey</a>, and rowing (the women's crew program is subject to the NCAA, while the men's rowing program is governed by its own administrative body, the <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a>). Under the Ivy League athletic agreement, the university does not offer <a href="/wiki/Athletic_scholarship" title="Athletic scholarship">athletic scholarships</a> for athletic recruiting.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornell University's <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team had at least a share of the national championship four times before 1940<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> and has won the Ivy League championship three times, last in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell's Men's Heavyweight Rowing program has won the national championship a record 38 times (12 under the <a href="/wiki/Rowing_Association_of_American_Colleges" title="Rowing Association of American Colleges">RAAC</a> format and 26 under the <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">IRA</a> format), making it one of the most successful athletic programs in the history of intercollegiate sports. The Cornell Men's Ice Hockey team has won the national championship twice.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cornelliana">Cornelliana</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cornelliana">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dragonday_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/Dragonday_2008.jpg/220px-Dragonday_2008.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/Dragonday_2008.jpg/330px-Dragonday_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/57/Dragonday_2008.jpg/440px-Dragonday_2008.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dragonday_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A tradition started in 1901, 
        <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Day" title="Dragon Day">Dragon Day</a> celebrates a feat by first-year 
        <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University_College_of_Architecture,_Art,_and_Planning" title="Cornell University College of Architecture, Art, and Planning">architecture</a> students to construct a colossal dragon to be paraded to center campus and then burned.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg/220px-Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg" width="220" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg/330px-Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg/440px-Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ezra_Cornell_emblem_with_motto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An ivy-covered emblem of 
        <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Cornell" title="Ezra Cornell">Ezra Cornell</a> circumscribed by the university motto
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Cornelliana" title="Cornelliana">Cornelliana</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Cornelliana is a term for Cornell's traditions, legends, and lore. Cornellian traditions include <a href="/wiki/Slope_Day" title="Slope Day">Slope Day</a>, a celebration held on the last day of classes of the spring semester, and <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Day" title="Dragon Day">Dragon Day</a>, which includes the burning of a dragon built by architecture students. Dragon Day is one of the school's oldest traditions and has been celebrated annually since 1901, typically on or near St. Patrick's Day. The dragon is built secretly by the architecture students, and taunting messages are left for the engineering students for the week before Dragon Day. On Dragon Day, the dragon is paraded across the Arts Quad and then set afire.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to legend, if a virgin crosses the <a href="/wiki/Arts_Quad" title="Arts Quad" class="mw-redirect">Arts Quad</a> at midnight, the statues of <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Cornell" title="Ezra Cornell">Ezra Cornell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Dickson_White" title="Andrew Dickson White">Andrew Dickson White</a> will walk off their pedestals, meet in the center of the Quad, and shake hands, congratulating themselves on the chastity of students. There is also another myth that if a couple crosses the suspension bridge on North Campus, and the young woman does not accept a kiss from her partner, the bridge will fall. If the kiss is accepted, the couple is assured a long future together.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is also host to various student pranks. For example, on at least two different occasions the university has awoken to find something odd atop the 173-foot (52.7&nbsp;m) tall McGraw clock tower—once a 60-pound (27&nbsp;kg) pumpkin and another time a disco ball. Because there is no access to the spire atop the tower, how the items were put in place remains a mystery.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> The colors of the lights on McGraw tower change to orange for Halloween and green for St. Patrick's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> The clock tower also plays music.</p> 
     <p>The school colors are <a href="/wiki/Carnelian_(color)" title="Carnelian (color)">carnelian</a> (a shade of red) and white, a play on &quot;Cornellian&quot; and Andrew Dickson White. A bear is commonly used as the unofficial mascot, which dates back to the introduction of the mascot &quot;Touchdown&quot; in 1915, a live bear who was brought onto the field during football games.<sup id="cite_ref-mascot_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mascot-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's <a href="/wiki/Alma_mater" title="Alma mater">alma mater</a> is &quot;<a href="/wiki/Far_Above_Cayuga%27s_Waters" title="Far Above Cayuga's Waters">Far Above Cayuga's Waters</a>&quot;, and its <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> is &quot;<a href="/wiki/Give_My_Regards_to_Davy" title="Give My Regards to Davy">Give My Regards to Davy</a>&quot;. People associated with the university are called &quot;Cornellians&quot;.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Cornell offers a variety of professional and peer counseling services to students.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> Gannett Clinic offers on-campus outpatient health services with emergency services and residential treatment provided by Cayuga Medical Center.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> For most of its history, Cornell provided residential medical care for sick students, including at the historic Sage Infirmary.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell offers specialized reproductive health and family planning services.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university received worldwide attention for a series of six student suicides that occurred during the 2009–10 school year, and they have since added temporary fences to its bridges while more permanent measures are in process. Before this abnormal cluster of suicides, the suicide rate at Cornell had been similar to or below the suicide rates of other American universities, including a period between 2005 and 2008 in which no suicides occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_Cornell_University" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with Cornell University">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with Cornell University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell counts numerous notable individuals who have either come to the university as faculty to teach and to conduct research, or as students who have gone on to do noteworthy things. In total, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation#Cornell_University" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">41 Nobel laureates</a> have been affiliated with Cornell as faculty or students.<sup id="cite_ref-nobel_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell1916Faculty.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Cornell1916Faculty.jpg/220px-Cornell1916Faculty.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Cornell1916Faculty.jpg/330px-Cornell1916Faculty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Cornell1916Faculty.jpg/440px-Cornell1916Faculty.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornell1916Faculty.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 1916 Cornell faculty
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cornell_University_faculty" title="List of Cornell University faculty">List of Cornell University faculty</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Cornell had 1,639 full-and part-time faculty members affiliated with its main campus,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> 1,235 affiliated with its New York City divisions, and 34 affiliated with its campus in Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Cornell's faculty for the 2005–06 academic year included three <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureates</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Crafoord_Prize" title="Crafoord Prize">Crafoord Prize</a> winner, two <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a> winners, a <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a> winner, two <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honor" title="Legion of Honor" class="mw-redirect">Legion of Honor</a> recipients, a <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Prize" title="World Food Prize">World Food Prize</a> winner, an <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Sakharov_Prize" title="Andrei Sakharov Prize" class="mw-redirect">Andrei Sakharov Prize</a> winner, three <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> winners, two <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Prize" title="Wolf Prize">Wolf Prize</a> winners, five <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_award" title="MacArthur award" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur award</a> winners, four <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, a <a href="/wiki/Carter_G._Woodson" title="Carter G. Woodson">Carter G. Woodson</a> Scholars Medallion recipient, 20 <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> career grant holders, a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a> Award, a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/American_Mathematical_Society" title="American Mathematical Society">American Mathematical Society</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Steele_Prize_for_Lifetime_Achievement" title="Steele Prize for Lifetime Achievement" class="mw-redirect">Steele Prize for Lifetime Achievement</a>, a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Heineman_Prize_for_Mathematical_Physics" title="Heineman Prize for Mathematical Physics" class="mw-redirect">Heineman Prize for Mathematical Physics</a>, and three <a href="/wiki/Packard_Foundation" title="Packard Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Packard Foundation</a> grant holders.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Kurt_Lewin" title="Kurt Lewin">Kurt Lewin</a> taught at Cornell from 1933 to 1935 and is considered the &quot;father of <a href="/wiki/Social_psychology" title="Social psychology">social psychology</a>&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Norman_Borlaug" title="Norman Borlaug">Norman Borlaug</a> taught at the university from 1982 to 1988 and is considered the &quot;father of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a>&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> being awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Gold_Medal" title="Congressional Gold Medal">Congressional Gold Medal</a>, and 49 honorary doctorates.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frances_Perkins" title="Frances Perkins">Frances Perkins</a> joined the Cornell faculty in 1952 after serving as the first female member of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Cabinet" title="United States Cabinet" class="mw-redirect">United States Cabinet</a> and served until her death in 1965. Perkins was a witness to the <a href="/wiki/Triangle_Shirtwaist_Factory_fire" title="Triangle Shirtwaist Factory fire">Triangle Shirtwaist Factory fire</a> in her adolescence and went on to champion the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Act" title="National Labor Relations Act">National Labor Relations Act</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Labor_Standards_Act" title="Fair Labor Standards Act">Fair Labor Standards Act</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_Act" title="Social Security Act">Social Security Act</a> while <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Labor" title="United States Secretary of Labor">United States Secretary of Labor</a>. <a href="/wiki/Buckminster_Fuller" title="Buckminster Fuller">Buckminster Fuller</a> was a visiting professor at Cornell for one year (1952),<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Louis_Gates" title="Henry Louis Gates">Henry Louis Gates</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_American_Studies" title="African American Studies" class="mw-redirect">African American Studies</a> scholar and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Louis_Gates_arrest_controversy" title="Henry Louis Gates arrest controversy">subject of an arrest controversy and White House &quot;Beer Summit&quot;</a>, taught at Cornell from 1985 to 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Primetime_Emmy_Award_for_Outstanding_Guest_Actor_in_a_Comedy_Series" title="Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Guest Actor in a Comedy Series">Emmy Award</a>-winning actor <a href="/wiki/John_Cleese" title="John Cleese">John Cleese</a>, known for his roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python" title="Monty Python">Monty Python</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" title="James Bond (film series)" class="mw-redirect">James Bond</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)">Harry Potter</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_(franchise)" title="Shrek (franchise)">Shrek</a></i>, has taught at Cornell since 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Evans_Hughes" title="Charles Evans Hughes">Charles Evans Hughes</a> taught in the law school from 1893 to 1895 before becoming <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">Chief Justice of the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgios_Papanikolaou" title="Georgios Papanikolaou">Georgios Papanikolaou</a>, who taught at Cornell's medical school from 1913 to 1961, invented the <a href="/wiki/Pap_test" title="Pap test">Pap smear</a> test for <a href="/wiki/Cervical_cancer" title="Cervical cancer">cervical cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a> was a professor at the university from 1968 to 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> He narrated and co-wrote the PBS series <i><a href="/wiki/Cosmos:_A_Personal_Voyage" title="Cosmos: A Personal Voyage">Cosmos</a></i>, the Emmy- and Peabody-award-winning show that became the most watched series in public-television history. He also wrote the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Contact_(novel)" title="Contact (novel)">Contact</a></i>, the basis for a 1997 <a href="/wiki/Contact_(film)" title="Contact (film)">film of the same name</a>, and he won a <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> for his novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dragons_of_Eden" title="The Dragons of Eden">The Dragons of Eden: Speculations on the Evolution of Human Intelligence</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/M._H._Abrams" title="M. H. Abrams">M. H. Abrams</a> is a professor emeritus of English and was the founding editor of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Norton_Anthology_of_English_Literature" title="The Norton Anthology of English Literature">The Norton Anthology of English Literature</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_L._Hoard" title="James L. Hoard">James L. Hoard</a>, a scientist who worked on the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a></p> 
     <p>Cornell has twice (2008 and 2009) been named a &quot;Great College to Work For&quot; by <a href="/wiki/The_Chronicle_of_Higher_Education" title="The Chronicle of Higher Education">The Chronicle of Higher Education</a>, due to receiving high ratings in <a href="/wiki/Compensation_and_benefits" title="Compensation and benefits">compensation and benefits</a>, connection to institution and pride, faculty-administration relations, job satisfaction, and post-retirement benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-bestemployer2009_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bestemployer2009-258"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p><br /></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cornell_University_alumni" title="List of Cornell University alumni">List of Cornell University alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Cornell counted 245,027 living alumni as of August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Its alumni constitute 31&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholarship" title="Marshall Scholarship">Marshall Scholars</a> and 28&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rhodes_Scholars_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhodes_Scholars-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> and Cornell is the only university with three female winners (<a href="/wiki/Pearl_S._Buck" title="Pearl S. Buck">Pearl S. Buck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_McClintock" title="Barbara McClintock">Barbara McClintock</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toni_Morrison" title="Toni Morrison">Toni Morrison</a>) of unshared <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prizes" title="Nobel Prizes" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Prizes</a> among its graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-nobel_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> Many alumni maintain university ties through <a href="/wiki/Homecoming" title="Homecoming">Homecoming</a>'s reunion weekend, through <i>Cornell Magazine</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> and through the <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Club_of_New_York" title="Cornell Club of New York">Cornell Club of New York</a>. In 2005, Cornell ranked #3 nationwide for gifts and bequests from alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cornellclubnyc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cornellclubnyc.jpg/220px-Cornellclubnyc.jpg" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cornellclubnyc.jpg/330px-Cornellclubnyc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Cornellclubnyc.jpg/440px-Cornellclubnyc.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cornellclubnyc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Cornell_Club" title="Cornell Club" class="mw-redirect">Cornell Club</a> in 
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> is a focal point for alumni.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Cornellians are noted for their accomplishments in public, professional, and corporate life.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_4-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lee_Teng-hui" title="Lee Teng-hui">Lee Teng-hui</a> was president of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mario_Garc%C3%ADa_Menocal" title="Mario Garc&iacute;a Menocal">Mario Garc&iacute;a Menocal</a> was president of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jamshid_Amuzegar" title="Jamshid Amuzegar" class="mw-redirect">Jamshid Amuzegar</a> ('50) was prime minister of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bill1989_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bill1989-264"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hu_Shih" title="Hu Shih">Hu Shih</a> ('14) was a Chinese reformer and representative to the United Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Janet_Reno" title="Janet Reno">Janet Reno</a> ('60) was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_female_United_States_Cabinet_Secretaries" title="List of female United States Cabinet Secretaries">first female</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">United States Attorney General</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-DuffyLeeman2005_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DuffyLeeman2005-266"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg" title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a> ('54) serves on the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bredeson1995_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bredeson1995-267"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup> Alumnus <a href="/wiki/David_Starr_Jordan" title="David Starr Jordan">David Starr Jordan</a> (1872) was the founding president of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Bishop122_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bishop122-268"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/M._Carey_Thomas" title="M. Carey Thomas">M. Carey Thomas</a> (1877) founded <a href="/wiki/Bryn_Mawr_College" title="Bryn Mawr College">Bryn Mawr College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Horowitz1999_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz1999-269"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, alumnus <a href="/wiki/Matt_Urban" title="Matt Urban">Matt Urban</a> ('41) holds the distinction as the most decorated serviceman in United States history.<sup id="cite_ref-Boven2000_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boven2000-270"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Cornellians in business include: <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Sanford_Weill" title="Sanford Weill" class="mw-redirect">Sanford Weill</a> ('55),<sup id="cite_ref-K42_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K42-271"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs_Group" title="Goldman Sachs Group" class="mw-redirect">Goldman Sachs Group</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Friedman_(PFIAB)" title="Stephen Friedman (PFIAB)">Stephen Friedman</a> ('59),<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kraft_Foods" title="Kraft Foods">Kraft Foods</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Irene_Rosenfeld" title="Irene Rosenfeld">Irene Rosenfeld</a> ('75, '77, '80),<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aetna" title="Aetna">Aetna</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bertolini" title="Mark Bertolini">Mark Bertolini</a> ('84),<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/S._C._Johnson_%26_Son" title="S. C. Johnson &amp; Son">S.C. Johnson &amp; Son</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Fisk_Johnson_III" title="Herbert Fisk Johnson III">Fisk Johnson</a> ('79, '80, '82, '84, '86),<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cargill" title="Cargill">Cargill</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Warren_Staley" title="Warren Staley">Warren Staley</a> ('67),<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_T._Derr" title="Kenneth T. Derr">Kenneth T. Derr</a> ('59),<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Nextel" title="Sprint Nextel" class="mw-redirect">Sprint Nextel</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Dan_Hesse" title="Dan Hesse" class="mw-redirect">Dan Hesse</a> ('77),<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Verizon" title="Verizon" class="mw-redirect">Verizon</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Lowell_McAdam" title="Lowell McAdam">Lowell McAdam</a> ('76),<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mastercard" title="Mastercard" class="mw-redirect">Mastercard</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Robert_Selander" title="Robert Selander">Robert Selander</a> ('72),<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coors_Brewing_Company" title="Coors Brewing Company">Coors Brewing Company</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Coors" title="Adolph Coors">Adolph Coors</a> ('37),<sup id="cite_ref-Bishop509_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bishop509-281"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Loews_Corporation" title="Loews Corporation">Loews Corporation</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Tisch" title="Andrew Tisch">Andrew Tisch</a> ('71),<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baupost_Group" title="Baupost Group">Baupost Group</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Seth_Klarman" title="Seth Klarman">Seth Klarman</a> ('79),<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> founder <a href="/wiki/James_McLamore" title="James McLamore">James McLamore</a> ('47),<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hotels.com" title="Hotels.com">Hotels.com</a> founder <a href="/wiki/David_Litman" title="David Litman">David Litman</a> ('79),<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PeopleSoft" title="PeopleSoft">PeopleSoft</a> founder <a href="/wiki/David_Duffield" title="David Duffield">David Duffield</a> ('62),<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Priceline.com" title="Priceline.com">Priceline.com</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Jay_S._Walker" title="Jay S. Walker">Jay Walker</a> ('77),<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Staples,_Inc." title="Staples, Inc." class="mw-redirect">Staples</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Myra_Hart" title="Myra Hart">Myra Hart</a> ('62),<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Irwin_M._Jacobs" title="Irwin M. Jacobs">Irwin M. Jacobs</a> ('56),<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tata_Group" title="Tata Group">Tata Group</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Ratan_Tata" title="Ratan Tata">Ratan Tata</a> ('62).<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In medicine, alumnus <a href="/wiki/Robert_Atkins_(nutritionist)" title="Robert Atkins (nutritionist)">Robert Atkins</a> ('55) developed the <a href="/wiki/Atkins_Diet" title="Atkins Diet" class="mw-redirect">Atkins Diet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Heimlich" title="Henry Heimlich">Henry Heimlich</a> ('47) developed the <a href="/wiki/Heimlich_maneuver" title="Heimlich maneuver" class="mw-redirect">Heimlich maneuver</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Greatbatch" title="Wilson Greatbatch">Wilson Greatbatch</a> ('50) invented the <a href="/wiki/Artificial_pacemaker" title="Artificial pacemaker" class="mw-redirect">pacemaker</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Maas" title="James Maas">James Maas</a> ('66; also a faculty member) coined the term &quot;<a href="/wiki/Power_nap" title="Power nap">power nap</a>&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/C._Everett_Koop" title="C. Everett Koop">C. Everett Koop</a> ('41) served as <a href="/wiki/Surgeon_General_of_the_United_States" title="Surgeon General of the United States">Surgeon General of the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A number of Cornellians have been prominent innovators. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Midgley,_Jr." title="Thomas Midgley, Jr.">Thomas Midgley, Jr.</a> ('11) invented <a href="/wiki/Freon" title="Freon">Freon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jon_Rubinstein" title="Jon Rubinstein">Jon Rubinstein</a> ('78) is credited with the development of the <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Tappan_Morris" title="Robert Tappan Morris">Robert Tappan Morris</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Morris_(computer_worm)" title="Morris (computer worm)" class="mw-redirect">first computer worm</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>. Eight Cornellians have served as <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronauts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Squyres" title="Steve Squyres">Steve Squyres</a> ('81) is the principal investigator on the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover" title="Mars Exploration Rover">Mars Exploration Rover</a> Mission,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Nye" title="Bill Nye">Bill Nye</a> ('77) is well known as &quot;<a href="/wiki/Bill_Nye_the_Science_Guy" title="Bill Nye the Science Guy">The Science Guy</a>&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In literature, <a href="/wiki/Toni_Morrison" title="Toni Morrison">Toni Morrison</a> ('50; <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel laureate</a>) is well known for her novel <i><a href="/wiki/Beloved_(novel)" title="Beloved (novel)">Beloved</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_S._Buck" title="Pearl S. Buck">Pearl S. Buck</a> ('25; Nobel laureate) authored <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Earth" title="The Good Earth">The Good Earth</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pynchon" title="Thomas Pynchon">Thomas Pynchon</a> ('59) penned such canonical works of postwar American fiction as <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity%27s_Rainbow" title="Gravity's Rainbow">Gravity's Rainbow</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crying_of_Lot_49" title="The Crying of Lot 49">The Crying of Lot 49</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/E._B._White" title="E. B. White">E. B. White</a> ('21) authored <i><a href="/wiki/Charlotte%27s_Web" title="Charlotte's Web">Charlotte's Web</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Stuart_Little" title="Stuart Little">Stuart Little</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup> Media personalities who have graduated from Cornell include <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Ann_Coulter" title="Ann Coulter">Ann Coulter</a> ('84)<sup id="cite_ref-K41_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K41-302"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">liberals</a> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Maher" title="Bill Maher">Bill Maher</a> ('78) and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Olbermann" title="Keith Olbermann">Keith Olbermann</a> ('79).<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several Cornellians have also achieved critical acclaim in entertainment. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Reeve" title="Christopher Reeve">Christopher Reeve</a> ('74) played <i><a href="/wiki/Superman_(film)" title="Superman (film)">Superman</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-K42_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K42-271"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Morgan" title="Frank Morgan">Frank Morgan</a> was <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Oz)" title="Wizard (Oz)" class="mw-redirect">The Wizard of Oz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Smits" title="Jimmy Smits">Jimmy Smits</a> ('82) was in <i><a href="/wiki/Episode_II:_Attack_of_the_Clones" title="Episode II: Attack of the Clones" class="mw-redirect">Star Wars</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-K42_271-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K42-271"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_D._Moore" title="Ronald D. Moore">Ronald D. Moore</a> created the 2004 remake of <i><a href="/wiki/Battlestar_Galactica" title="Battlestar Galactica">Battlestar Galactica</a></i>. On the architectural front, alumnus <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Shreve" title="Richmond Shreve">Richmond Shreve</a> (1902) designed the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Raymond_M._Kennedy" title="Raymond M. Kennedy">Raymond M. Kennedy</a> ('15) designed <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a>'s famous <a href="/wiki/Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre" title="Grauman's Chinese Theatre" class="mw-redirect">Grauman's Chinese Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bishop399_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bishop399-305"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In athletics, Cornell graduates include football legend <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Scobey_Warner" title="Glenn Scobey Warner">Glenn &quot;Pop&quot; Warner</a> (1894),<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup> former head coach of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States men's national soccer team</a> <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Arena" title="Bruce Arena">Bruce Arena</a> ('73),<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> commissioner <a href="/wiki/Gary_Bettman" title="Gary Bettman">Gary Bettman</a> ('74),<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup> six-time <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> winning <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper" title="Goalkeeper">goalie</a> <a href="/wiki/Ken_Dryden" title="Ken Dryden">Ken Dryden</a> ('69)<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Raptors" title="Toronto Raptors">Toronto Raptors</a> president <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Colangelo" title="Bryan Colangelo">Bryan Colangelo</a> ('87).<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup> Alumni also include two-time <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Boothe" title="Kevin Boothe">Kevin Boothe</a>('05) and 1971 <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> runner-up <a href="/wiki/Ed_Marinaro" title="Ed Marinaro">Ed Marinaro</a> ('71).<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cornell_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The other is the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The University's charter was amended on April 24, 1867 to specify alumni elected trustees, (<span class="citation book">Waterman Thomas Hewett, Frank R. Holmes, Lewis A. Williams (1905). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=bPIKAAAAIAAJ&amp;dq=first%20alumni%20trustees%20cornell%20elect&amp;pg=PA278#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>Cornell University, a history, Volume 1</i></a>. University Publishing Society. p.&nbsp;278<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved December 14, 2010</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACornell+University&amp;rft.aulast=Waterman+Thomas+Hewett%2C+Frank+R.+Holmes%2C+Lewis+A.+Williams&amp;rft.au=Waterman+Thomas+Hewett%2C+Frank+R.+Holmes%2C+Lewis+A.+Williams&amp;rft.btitle=Cornell+University%2C+a+history%2C+Volume+1&amp;rft.date=1905&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DbPIKAAAAIAAJ%26dq%3Dfirst%2520alumni%2520trustees%2520cornell%2520elect%26pg%3DPA278%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.pages=278&amp;rft.pub=University+Publishing+Society&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span>) however that provision did not become operative until there were at least 100 alumni (<span class="citation book">(State), New York (1881). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/?id=DnQ4AAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA537&amp;dq=first+alumni+trustees+cornell+elect#v=onepage&amp;q=first%20alumni%20trustees%20cornell%20elect&amp;f=false"><i>The revised statutes of the State of New York</i></a>. p.&nbsp;537<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved December 14, 2010</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACornell+University&amp;rft.au=%28State%29%2C+New+York&amp;rft.aufirst=New+York&amp;rft.aulast=%28State%29&amp;rft.btitle=The+revised+statutes+of+the+State+of+New+York&amp;rft.date=1881&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3DDnQ4AAAAIAAJ%26pg%3DPA537%26dq%3Dfirst%2Balumni%2Btrustees%2Bcornell%2Belect%23v%3Donepage%26q%3Dfirst%2520alumni%2520trustees%2520cornell%2520elect%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.pages=537&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span> ) in 1872. (<span class="citation book">Frank Hatch Kasson, Frank Herbert Palmer, Raymond P. Palmer, Project Innovation (September 1901). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=jS05AAAAMAAJ&amp;dq=first%20alumni%20trustees%20cornell%20elect&amp;pg=PA107#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>Education, Volume 22</i></a>. pp.&nbsp;108–09<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved December 14, 2010</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACornell+University&amp;rft.au=Frank+Hatch+Kasson%2C+Frank+Herbert+Palmer%2C+Raymond+P.+Palmer%2C+Project+Innovation&amp;rft.aulast=Frank+Hatch+Kasson%2C+Frank+Herbert+Palmer%2C+Raymond+P.+Palmer%2C+Project+Innovation&amp;rft.btitle=Education%2C+Volume+22&amp;rft.date=September+1901&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DjS05AAAAMAAJ%26dq%3Dfirst%2520alumni%2520trustees%2520cornell%2520elect%26pg%3DPA107%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.pages=108%E2%80%9309&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span>) Also in 1865, the election of the Harvard University Board of Overseers was shifted to alumni voting.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Weill Cornell Medical College-NYC medical division units have additional external affiliations with 1,326&nbsp;full-time and part-time faculty members elsewhere.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources.
